II. Foreign candidates can be admitted to programmes and academic courses provided that they: hold visa or a residence card or a different document that certifies the legal stay of the candidate on the territory of the Republic of Poland; hold a health certificate stating that there are no objections for the candidate to study on a given faculty and in accordance with the selected form of education; hold a document certifying that the candidate has health insurance or accident insurance for the period of studying in Poland or holds the European Health Insurance Card or a declaration of purchasing the insurance in the National Health Fund [Narodowy Fundusz Zdrowia] immediately after starting education; holds a certificate of passing Polish secondary school-leaving exams (matura) or holds a validated document, a certificate with apostille or any other document issued abroad which entitles the candidate to start their education at any university in a country where such a document has been issued, pursuant to the regulations on the validation (nostrification) of school certificates and certificates of secondary school leaving exams obtained abroad or pursuant to an international agreement, can be considered equivalent to a respective Polish secondary school-leaving exams (matura) certificate. II. Foreign candidates can study in Polish provided that they: complete a one-year preparatory Polish language course delivered by one of the schools appointed for this purpose by a respective Minister of Science and Higher Education, or obtain a certificate issued by the State Commission for the Certification of Proficiency in Polish as a Foreign Language, or receive a confirmation from the Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska University that their command of Polish language is sufficient enough to study in Polish; demonstrate specific skills required by Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska University for starting education on a given"

Radziszewskiego 10 20-031 Lublin, Poland tel. (+48) 81 537 52 12 www.mfi.umcs.lublin.pl The Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science was established in 1989 as a result of transformation of the Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry into two separate faculties. It consists of three institutes: the Institute of Mathematics, the Institute of Physics, and the Institute of Computer Science. The Faculty trains specialists whose theoretical and applied knowledge acquired there ensures their very good position on the labor market. Its academic staff are engaged in intensive academic work under individual research grants, including highly prestigious Team and Pomost schemes, and as part of statutory research. The Faculty also cooperates with many centers at home and abroad, inter alia in Italy, USA, France, Germany, Israel, Finland, Ukraine, Russia, and Spain. The particular institutes of the Faculty organize a range of conferences and workshops on different subjects, the most popular being regular international conferences: Ion Implantation and Other Applications of Ions and Electrons (ION), Maria and Pierre Curie Nuclear Physics Workshops, Infinite Particle Systems, Computer Aspects of Numerical Algorithms (CANA), Information Science \u2013 Studies and Applications (IBIZA Conference), and Cryptography and Security Systems. Together with the Lublin Branch of Polish Mathematical Society and the Student Mathematicians Club \u201cAkademia Plato\u0144ska [Plato\u2019s Academy]\u201d the Institute of Mathematics has organized the \u201cSchool-Contest Winners Scientific Club\u201d for high-school students; it organizes the National Symposium of Young Mathematicians (for primary and junior high-school students), Mathematical Skirmishes (for high-school students),"

Foreign candidates can be admitted to programmes and academic courses provided that they: hold visa or a residence card or a different document that certifies the legal stay of the candidate on the territory of the Republic of Poland; hold a health certificate stating that there are no objections for the candidate to study on a given faculty and in accordance with the selected form of education; hold a document certifying that the candidate has health insurance or accident insurance for the period of studying in Poland or holds the European Health Insurance Card or a declaration of purchasing the insurance in the National Health Fund [Narodowy Fundusz Zdrowia] immediately after starting education; holds a certificate of passing Polish secondary school-leaving exams (matura) or holds a validated document, a certificate with apostille or any other document issued abroad which entitles the candidate to start their education at any university in a country where such a document has been issued, pursuant to the regulations on the validation (nostrification) of school certificates and certificates of secondary school leaving exams obtained abroad or pursuant to an international agreement, can be considered equivalent to a respective Polish secondary school-leaving exams (matura) certificate. II. Foreign candidates can study in Polish provided that they: complete a one-year preparatory Polish language course delivered by one of the schools appointed for this purpose by a respective Minister of Science and Higher Education, or obtain a certificate issued by the State Commission for the Certification of Proficiency in Polish as a Foreign Language, or receive a confirmation from the Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska University that their command of Polish language is sufficient enough to study in Polish; demonstrate specific skills required by Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska University for starting education on a given"

Listy kod\u00f3w dziedzin obowi\u0105zuj\u0105cej w programie Socrates/Erasmus, czwarta (dot\u0105d na og\u00f3\u0142 0) \u2013 ewentualne uszczeg\u00f3\u0142owienie informacji o dyscyplinie, pi\u0105ta \u2013 stopie\u0144 zaawansowania przedmiotu ustalony na podstawie roku studi\u00f3w, dla kt\u00f3rego przedmiot jest przeznaczony. / (0541) Matematyka Kod ISCED - Mi\u0119dzynarodowa Standardowa Klasyfikacja Kszta\u0142cenia (International Standard Classification of Education) zosta\u0142a opracowana przez UNESCO. Nazwa przedmiotu: Matematyka dyskretna Jednostka: Instytut Informatyki Grupy: Strona przedmiotu: http://matrix.umcs.lublin.pl/~akrajka/MD Punkty ECTS i inne: 0 LUB 4.00 (w zale\u017cno\u015bci od programu) Podstawowe informacje o zasadach przyporz\u0105dkowania punkt\u00f3w ECTS: roczny wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 dla danego etapu studi\u00f3w wynosi 1500-1800 h, co odpowiada 60 ECTS; tygodniowy wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta wynosi 45 h; 1 punkt ECTS odpowiada 25-30 godzinom pracy studenta potrzebnej do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119; tygodniowy nak\u0142ad pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 pozwala uzyska\u0107 1,5 ECTS; nak\u0142ad pracy potrzebny do zaliczenia przedmiotu, kt\u00f3remu przypisano 3 ECTS, stanowi 10% semestralnego obci\u0105\u017cenia studenta. zobacz regu\u0142y punktacji J\u0119zyk prowadzenia: polski Wymagania wst\u0119pne: 1. Znajomo\u015b\u0107 indukcji matematycznej 2. Umiej\u0119tno\u015b\u0107 obliczania pochodnych 3. Podstawy algebry 4. Podstawy logika 5. Podstawy teorii mnogo\u015bci Godzinowe ekwiwalenty punkt\u00f3w ECTS: 1. Godziny kontaktowe z nauczycielem akademickim -wyk\u0142ad 30, -konwersatorium 30, -konsultacje 2, -egzamin 3. Razem 65. 2. Samodzielna praca studenta - samodzielne rozwi\u0105zywanie zada\u0144 25, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do konwersatorium 15, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do egzaminu 15. Razem 55. Samodzielna praca studenta + godziny kontaktowe = 120 Liczba punkt\u00f3w ECTS - 4 w tym 2,17 za godziny kontaktowe oraz 1,83 za samodzieln\u0105 prac\u0119 student\u00f3w. Spos\u00f3b weryfikacji efekt\u00f3w kszta\u0142cenia: Kolokwia - W01 W02, W04, Egzamin - W01, W02, W04, Zadania wykonywane na konwersatorium - U01, U02, W01, W02, W03, W04, Pe\u0142ny opis: Matematyka dyskretna - to zbiorcza nazwa r\u00f3\u017cnych dzia\u0142\u00f3w matematyki, zajmuj\u0105cych si\u0119 badaniem struktur nieci\u0105g\u0142ych czyli sko\u0144czonych lub co najwy\u017cej przeliczalnych. Foreign candidates can be admitted to studies and training courses if they: have a visa or a residence card or another document certifying the legal stay of the candidate on the territory of the Republic of Poland have a health certificate stating that there are no objections for the candidate to study on a given faculty and in accordance with the selected form of education hold a document certifying that the candidate has health insurance or accident insurance for the period of studying in Poland or holds the European Health Insurance Card or a declaration of purchasing the insurance in the National Health Fund [Narodowy Fundusz Zdrowia] immediately after starting education II. Foreign candidates can study in Polish, if they: complete a one-year preparatory Polish language course delivered by one of the schools appointed for this purpose by a respective Minister of Science and Higher Education, or obtain a certificate issued by the State Commission for the Certification of Proficiency in Polish as a Foreign Language, or receive a confirmation from the Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska University that their command of Polish language is sufficient enough to study in Polish present an undergraduate higher education diploma issued in Poland or legalisation or apostille of a document confirming the graduation from a foreign higher education institution, ,certifieses that the holder has the right to apply for second-cycle (graduate) programmes in the country of the institution which issued the document. The document should, according to the regulations on the validation (nostrification) of school certificates and secondary school leaving exams obtained abroad or according to an international agreement, be possible to be recognized as equivalent to a respective Polish higher education diploma of the first-cycle study programme (undergraduate) demonstrate specific skills required by Maria Curie-Sk\u0142odowska Univers"

Radziszewskiego 10 20-031 Lublin, Poland tel. (+48) 81 537 52 12 www.mfi.umcs.lublin.pl The Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science was established in 1989 as a result of transformation of the Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry into two separate faculties. It consists of three institutes: the Institute of Mathematics, the Institute of Physics, and the Institute of Computer Science. The Faculty trains specialists whose theoretical and applied knowledge acquired there ensures their very good position on the labor market. Its academic staff are engaged in intensive academic work under individual research grants, including highly prestigious Team and Pomost schemes, and as part of statutory research. The Faculty also cooperates with many centers at home and abroad, inter alia in Italy, USA, France, Germany, Israel, Finland, Ukraine, Russia, and Spain. The particular institutes of the Faculty organize a range of conferences and workshops on different subjects, the most popular being regular international conferences: Ion Implantation and Other Applications of Ions and Electrons (ION), Maria and Pierre Curie Nuclear Physics Workshops, Infinite Particle Systems, Computer Aspects of Numerical Algorithms (CANA), Information Science \u2013 Studies and Applications (IBIZA Conference), and Cryptography and Security Systems. Together with the Lublin Branch of Polish Mathematical Society and the Student Mathematicians Club \u201cAkademia Plato\u0144ska [Plato\u2019s Academy]\u201d the Institute of Mathematics has organized the \u201cSchool-Contest Winners Scientific Club\u201d for high-school students; it organizes the National Symposium of Young Mathematicians (for primary and junior high-school students), Mathematical Skirmishes (for high-school students),"

    "title": "Algorytmy i struktury danych I - Przedmioty",
    "link": "https://usosweb.umcs.pl/kontroler.php?_action=katalog2/przedmioty/pokazPrzedmiot&prz_kod=MFI-I.2Z.042",
    "content": "Algorytmy i struktury danych I - Przedmioty - Uniwersytet Marii Curie-Sk\u0142odowskiej Uniwersytet Marii Curie-Sk\u0142odowskiej w Lublinie - Centralny System Uwierzytelniania NA SKR\u00d3TY STUDENCI, PRACOWNICY JEDNOSTKI ORGANIZACYJNE PRZEDMIOTY Algorytmy i struktury danych I STUDIA AKADEMIKI POMOC help Drukuj sylabus Algorytmy i struktury danych I Informacje og\u00f3lne Kod przedmiotu: MFI-I.2Z.042 Kod Erasmus / ISCED: (brak danych) / (brak danych) Nazwa przedmiotu: Algorytmy i struktury danych I Jednostka: Wydzia\u0142 Matematyki, Fizyki i Informatyki Grupy: Strona przedmiotu: https://kampus.umcs.pl/course/view.php?id=69 Punkty ECTS i inne: 0 LUB 6.00 (w zale\u017cno\u015bci od programu) Podstawowe informacje o zasadach przyporz\u0105dkowania punkt\u00f3w ECTS: roczny wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 dla danego etapu studi\u00f3w wynosi 1500-1800 h, co odpowiada 60 ECTS; tygodniowy wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta wynosi 45 h; 1 punkt ECTS odpowiada 25-30 godzinom pracy studenta potrzebnej do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119; tygodniowy nak\u0142ad pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 pozwala uzyska\u0107 1,5 ECTS; nak\u0142ad pracy potrzebny do zaliczenia przedmiotu, kt\u00f3remu przypisano 3 ECTS, stanowi 10% semestralnego obci\u0105\u017cenia studenta. zobacz regu\u0142y punktacji J\u0119zyk prowadzenia: polski Wymagania wst\u0119pne: Umiej\u0119tno\u015b\u0107 programowania w j\u0119zyku C++ oraz znajomo\u015b\u0107 podstaw matematyki. Przedmioty wprowadzaj\u0105ce: - Podstawy programowania. - Programowanie obiektowe. - Algebra liniowa z geometri\u0105, - Logika i teoria mnogo\u015bci - Matematyka dyskretna. Godzinowe ekwiwalenty punkt\u00f3w ECTS: 1. Godziny kontaktowe z nauczycielem akademickim -wyk\u0142ad 30, -laboratorium 30, -konsultacje 2, -egzamin 3. Razem 65. 2. Samodzielna praca studenta - samodzielne rozwi\u0105zywanie zada\u0144 programistycznych 55, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do laboratorium 15, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do egzaminu 15. Razem 85. Samodzielna praca studenta + godziny kontaktowe = 180 Liczba punkt\u00f3w ECTS - 6 w tym 2,17 za godziny kontaktowe oraz 3,83 za samodzieln\u0105 prac\u0119 student\u00f3w. Spos\u00f3b weryfikacji efekt\u00f3w kszta\u0142cenia: Kartk\u00f3wki - W1. Programy zaliczeniowe - W1, W2, U1, U2, K1, K2,K3. Aktywno\u015b\u0107 - K1. Egzamin przy komputerach - W1, U1, U2, K1. Pe\u0142ny opis: Zapoznanie student\u00f3w z podstawowymi strukturami danych i algorytmami. Wyrobienie u student\u00f3w umiej\u0119tno\u015bci tworzenia, analizy i implementacji prostych algorytm\u00f3w oraz ich wykorzystania do rozwi\u0105zywania problem\u00f3w wyst\u0119puj\u0105cych w praktyce. Laboratoria s\u0105 skorelowane z wyk\u0142adem. Utrwala si\u0119 na nich materia\u0142 poznany na wyk\u0142adzie i rozwi\u0105zuje zadania algorytmiczne zwi\u0105zane z tematami poszczeg\u00f3lnych wyk\u0142ad\u00f3w. Zakres materia\u0142u: 1. Elementy teorii z\u0142o\u017cono\u015bci obliczeniowej. 2. Abstrakcyjne typy danych i algorytmy operuj\u0105ce na nich: a) lista, b) kolejka, c) stos, d) kolejka priorytetowa, e) drzewo, f) graf. 2. Sortowanie. 3. Metody konstruowania algorytm\u00f3w: a) algorytmy zach\u0142anne, b) programowanie dynamiczne, c) metoda ,,dzi"

Menu Start Applicant Student International Alumni Doctoral Schools International Research Exchanges Polish courses more About UMCS Faculties Faculty of Arts Faculty of Biology and Biotechnology Faculty of Chemistry Faculty of Economics Faculty of Languages, Literatures and Cultures Faculty of Philosophy and Sociology Faculty of History and Archaeology Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science Faculty of Earth Sciences and Spatial Management Faculty of Education and Psychology Faculty of Political Science and Journalism Faculty of Law and Administration UMCS Branch Campus in Pu\u0142awy Contact Submenu Find Find Contrast A A A A A A + A ++ Site map EN arrow PL RU UA AZ Main page Faculties Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science Print Report an error Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science FACULTY OF MATHEMATICS, PHYSICS AND COMPUTER SCIENCE ul. Radziszewskiego 10 20-031 Lublin, Poland tel. (+48) 81 537 52 12 www.mfi.umcs.lublin.pl The Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Computer Science was established in 1989 as a result of transformation of the Faculty of Mathematics, Physics and Chemistry into two separate faculties. It consists of three institutes: the Institute of Mathematics, the Institute of Physics, and the Institute of Computer Science. The Faculty trains specialists whose theoretical and applied knowledge acquired there ensures their very good position on the labor market. Its academic staff are engaged in intensive academic work under individual research grants, including highly prestigious Team and Pomost schemes, and as part of statutory research. The Faculty also cooperates with many centers at home and abroad, inter alia in Italy, USA, France, Germany, Israel, Finland, Ukraine, Russia, and Spain. The particular institutes of the Faculty organize a range of conferences and workshops on different subjects, the most popular being regular international conferences: Ion Implantation and Other Applications of Ions and Electrons (ION), Maria and Pierre Curie Nuclear Physics Workshops, Infinite Particle Systems, Computer Aspects of Numerical Algorithms (CANA), Information Science \u2013 Studies and Applications (IBIZA Conference), and Cryptography and Security Systems. Together with the Lublin Branch of Polish Mathematical Society and the Student Mathematicians Club \u201cAkademia Plato\u0144ska [Plato\u2019s Academy]\u201d the Institute of Mathematics has organized the \u201cSchool-Contest Winners Scientific Club\u201d for high-school students; it organizes the National Symposium of Young Mathematicians (for primary and junior high-school students), Mathematical Skirmishes (for high-school students),"

    "content": "Matematyka dyskretna - Przedmioty - Uniwersytet Marii Curie-Sk\u0142odowskiej Uniwersytet Marii Curie-Sk\u0142odowskiej w Lublinie - Centralny System Uwierzytelniania NA SKR\u00d3TY STUDENCI, PRACOWNICY JEDNOSTKI ORGANIZACYJNE PRZEDMIOTY Matematyka dyskretna STUDIA AKADEMIKI POMOC help Drukuj sylabus Matematyka dyskretna Informacje og\u00f3lne Kod przedmiotu: MFI-I.1L.011 Kod Erasmus / ISCED: 11.1 Kod klasyfikacyjny przedmiotu sk\u0142ada si\u0119 z trzech do pi\u0119ciu cyfr, przy czym trzy pierwsze oznaczaj\u0105 klasyfikacj\u0119 dziedziny wg. Listy kod\u00f3w dziedzin obowi\u0105zuj\u0105cej w programie Socrates/Erasmus, czwarta (dot\u0105d na og\u00f3\u0142 0) \u2013 ewentualne uszczeg\u00f3\u0142owienie informacji o dyscyplinie, pi\u0105ta \u2013 stopie\u0144 zaawansowania przedmiotu ustalony na podstawie roku studi\u00f3w, dla kt\u00f3rego przedmiot jest przeznaczony. / (0541) Matematyka Kod ISCED - Mi\u0119dzynarodowa Standardowa Klasyfikacja Kszta\u0142cenia (International Standard Classification of Education) zosta\u0142a opracowana przez UNESCO. Nazwa przedmiotu: Matematyka dyskretna Jednostka: Instytut Informatyki Grupy: Strona przedmiotu: http://matrix.umcs.lublin.pl/~akrajka/MD Punkty ECTS i inne: 0 LUB 4.00 (w zale\u017cno\u015bci od programu) Podstawowe informacje o zasadach przyporz\u0105dkowania punkt\u00f3w ECTS: roczny wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 dla danego etapu studi\u00f3w wynosi 1500-1800 h, co odpowiada 60 ECTS; tygodniowy wymiar godzinowy nak\u0142adu pracy studenta wynosi 45 h; 1 punkt ECTS odpowiada 25-30 godzinom pracy studenta potrzebnej do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119; tygodniowy nak\u0142ad pracy studenta konieczny do osi\u0105gni\u0119cia zak\u0142adanych efekt\u00f3w uczenia si\u0119 pozwala uzyska\u0107 1,5 ECTS; nak\u0142ad pracy potrzebny do zaliczenia przedmiotu, kt\u00f3remu przypisano 3 ECTS, stanowi 10% semestralnego obci\u0105\u017cenia studenta. zobacz regu\u0142y punktacji J\u0119zyk prowadzenia: polski Wymagania wst\u0119pne: 1. Znajomo\u015b\u0107 indukcji matematycznej 2. Umiej\u0119tno\u015b\u0107 obliczania pochodnych 3. Podstawy algebry 4. Podstawy logika 5. Podstawy teorii mnogo\u015bci Godzinowe ekwiwalenty punkt\u00f3w ECTS: 1. Godziny kontaktowe z nauczycielem akademickim -wyk\u0142ad 30, -konwersatorium 30, -konsultacje 2, -egzamin 3. Razem 65. 2. Samodzielna praca studenta - samodzielne rozwi\u0105zywanie zada\u0144 25, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do konwersatorium 15, - przygotowanie si\u0119 do egzaminu 15. Razem 55. Samodzielna praca studenta + godziny kontaktowe = 120 Liczba punkt\u00f3w ECTS - 4 w tym 2,17 za godziny kontaktowe oraz 1,83 za samodzieln\u0105 prac\u0119 student\u00f3w. Spos\u00f3b weryfikacji efekt\u00f3w kszta\u0142cenia: Kolokwia - W01 W02, W04, Egzamin - W01, W02, W04, Zadania wykonywane na konwersatorium - U01, U02, W01, W02, W03, W04, Pe\u0142ny opis: Matematyka dyskretna - to zbiorcza nazwa r\u00f3\u017cnych dzia\u0142\u00f3w matematyki, zajmuj\u0105cych si\u0119 badaniem struktur nieci\u0105g\u0142ych czyli sko\u0144czonych lub co najwy\u017cej przeliczalnych. Sta\u0142a si\u0119 popularna w ostatnich latach dzi\u0119ki zastosowaniom w informatyce, kt\u00f3ra w spos\u00f3b naturalny zajmuje si\u0119 jedynie strukturami sko\u0144czonymi (sko\u0144czona reprezentacja liczb, sko\u0144czona ilo\u015b\u0107 operacji "

    "link": "https://www.famnit.upr.si/en/education/undergraduate/math-first/",
    "content": "Mathematics - UP FAMNIT UP FAMNIT University of Primorska Faculty of Mathematics, Natural Sciences and Information Technologies --> SI | EN First page > Education > Undergraduate Studies > Mathematics Mathematics print General information Programme coordinator About the programme Educational and professional goals Course structure Elective courses and study fields Admission requirements Continuation of studies according to the transfer criteria Advancement requirements Graduate competencies Graduate employment opportunities Math department's yearly report: Report 2014 Report 2013 Report 2012 Report 2011 General information Name of the programme: Mathematics Type of programme: academic, 1st Bologna cycle Degree awarded: \"diplomirani matematik (UN)\" equiv. to B.Sc. in Mathematics Duration: 3 years (6 semesters) ECTS-credits: 180 Programme structure: 30 courses (9 electives) Mode of study: full-time Language of study: Slovene, English Programme coordinator top Prof. Marko Orel, PhD For information regarding application, enrolment and other administrative procedures please contact Student Services . About the programme top Welcome to Famnit Mathematics is the only universal language of interpersonal communication which is present everywhere in the world and at all levels of education. It is the foundation of all science and an indispensable tool in the social sciences and economics. As the theoretical core of computer science, its influence is growing in all areas of life that will decisively mark the 21st Century. Among these are modern economics, communications, data security, national security, and the decoding of the human genome and human brain. The first half of the study year and the second study year are mainly devoted to the learning and consolidation of the fundamentals of analysis, algebra, discrete mathematics and numerical computing. Along the way, students will learn a set of computer skills and the basics of probability theory. Within the labour market for the financial sector, the latter represents an important advantage for mathematics students versus students who come from management-/economy-oriented studies. Moreover, the computer-oriented courses, along with computer-oriented ways of thinking that an individual develops while studying mathematics, provide a good foundation for employment in programming and related companies. The larger part of the study programme represents elective courses where students learn about various specific areas of pure and applied mathematics. An optional part of the curriculum also has an interdisciplinary outline, which means that students can choose courses where the natural sciences (especially biology and biochemistry) combine with computer science and mathematics. Since virtually every science (at the research level) significantly relies on mathematics, mathematics undergraduate studies are also suitable for those who will later shift to other sciences. I want to receive exclusive email updates from YourDictionary. Sign in with Google By signing in, you agree to our Terms and Conditions and Privacy Policy . Success! We'll see you in your inbox soon. Thank you! Undo Grammar Punctuation What Are the 16 Punctuation Marks in English Grammar? By Jennifer Gunner, M.Ed. Education , Senior Writer Updated October 4, 2022 Image Credits DESCRIPTION tourist illustration with punctuation marks sentence example SOURCE girl: Rudzhan Nagiev / iStock / Getty Images Plus / background: Tolchik / iStock / Getty Images Plus / via Getty created by YourDictionary PERMISSION Used under Getty Images license In English, there are 16 punctuation marks \u2014 the period, question mark, exclamation point, comma, semicolon, colon, em dash, en dash, hyphen, parentheses, brackets, braces, apostrophe, double quotation marks, single quotation marks, and ellipsis \u2014 and they\u2019re not as scary as they sound. Each punctuation mark has a specific use and purpose in a sentence's structure. In this article Period ( . ) Question Mark ( ? ) Exclamation Point ( ! ) Comma ( , ) Semicolon ( ; ) Colon ( : ) Em Dash ( \u2014 ) En Dash ( \u2013 ) Hyphen ( - ) Parentheses ( ) Brackets [ ] Braces { } Apostrophe ( \u2018 ) Quotation Marks (\u201c \u201d) Single Quotation Marks (\u2018 \u2019) Ellipsis (...) Punctuation Marks Reference Poster British vs. American English Punctuation Period ( . ) The . is called a period. The period actually serves two purposes in grammar. When it appears at the end of a declarative sentence , it ends the sentence. The period can also indicate that a word is an abbreviation. As a sentence ender - Jane and Jack went to the market . After an abbreviation - John Jones Jr . was born on Dec . 6, 2008. Question Mark ( ? ) The ? is called a question mark. Question marks ask direct questions, which are also known as interrogative sentences . They can also express confusion. Interrogative sentence - When did Jane leave for the market ? Expressing confusion - Why do we have so much homework ? Exclamation Point ( ! ) The ! is called an exclamation point. Exclamation points are punctuation marks that show a sudden outcry in writing. They also emphasize a point more strongly than a period. Sudden outcry - \"Holy cow ! \" scr"

    "title": "Basic Estonian Words and Phrases",
    "link": "https://lingvist.com/course/learn-estonian-online/resources/basic-estonian-words-and-phrases/",
    "content": "Basic Estonian Words and Phrases | Lingvist Lingvist Home Classroom BETA Custom Decks Education Students Educators Business Pricing Blog Display language: English espa\u00f1ol fran\u00e7ais \u0440\u0443\u0441\u0441\u043a\u0438\u0439 portugu\u00eas Deutsch eesti Portugu\u00eas (BR) Nederlands Italiano \u7b80\u4f53\u4e2d\u6587 \u7e41\u9ad4\u4e2d\u6587 \u0423\u043a\u0440\u0430\u0457\u043d\u0441\u044c\u043a\u0430 Polski \u65e5\u672c\u8a9e \u0627\u0644\u0639\u0631\u0628\u064a\u0629 Sign up Log in Lingvist Home Classroom BETA Custom Decks Education Students Educators Business Pricing Blog Sign up Log in EN English espa\u00f1ol fran\u00e7ais \u0440\u0443\u0441\u0441\u043a\u0438\u0439 portugu\u00eas Deutsch eesti Portugu\u00eas (BR) Nederlands Italiano \u7b80\u4f53\u4e2d\u6587 \u7e41\u9ad4\u4e2d\u6587 \u0423\u043a\u0440\u0430\u0457\u043d\u0441\u044c\u043a\u0430 Polski \u65e5\u672c\u8a9e \u0627\u0644\u0639\u0631\u0628\u064a\u0629 Basic Estonian Words and Phrases If you plan to travel to Estonia or want to learn the Estonian language , then this article is the perfect starting point. You\u2019ll find some essential Estonian words and phrases here that are useful to know, no matter what your goal for learning Estonian might be. Having a grasp of useful Estonian expressions can greatly enhance your travel experience and give you valuable knowledge about the country\u2019s culture and traditions. Additionally, these phrases can lead to great conversations and foster connections with the locals. If you mostly plan to spend your time in Tallinn, then you\u2019ll find that almost everyone among the younger generations can speak English, but if you venture out of Tallinn and Harju County, then it might be useful to know some Estonian to help you communicate with the locals. Learn with Lingvist now Get started Greetings and Farewells in Estonian Estonians don\u2019t expect foreigners to understand or speak their language, so learning and using even some basic Estonian is going to make them happy, although they might not express it. Let\u2019s start with some greetings and goodbyes. Tere \u2013 Hello. This is the most common way of greeting someone in Estonian and can be used both formally and informally. Tervist \u2013 Hello. A less formal greeting, so it\u2019s better to use it when you\u2019ve met the person before. When you say \u201c Tervist ,\u201d you\u2019re literally wishing someone health. Hei \u2013 Hey. Even less formal than \u201c Tervist .\u201d N\u00e4gemist \u2013 Goodbye. Head aega \u2013 Goodbye. T\u0161au \u2013 Ciao. Used with people who you know as both a greeting and a goodbye. The correct way of writing it is \u201c T\u0161au ,\u201d but when you see Estonians type this word, then you\u2019ll very rarely see someone use the correct form, since it\u2019s easier just to write \u201c Tsau .\u201d Examples: T\u0161au, kuidas l\u00e4heb? \u2013 Hey, how are you doing? Ma hakkan siis minema. T\u0161au! \u2013 I\u2019ll get going then. Bye! T\u0161auki \u2013 A cuter way of saying \u201c T\u0161au .\u201d Homseni \u2013 Until tomorrow. You can use this when you know that you\u2019ll see this person tomorrow. J\u00e4rgmise korrani \u2013 Until next time Kohtumiseni \u2013 Until next time. The literal meaning is \u201cUntil (we) meet.\u201d N\u00e4gudeni \u2013 Until next time. The literal translation is \u201cUntil faces.\u201d Pakaa \u2013 Bye. More slangish-sounding and borrowed from Russian. Example: T\u0161au, pakaa, varsti n\u00e4eme! \u2013 Bye, see you soon! Meeldiv tutvuda \u2013 Nice to meet you. Literally \u201cNice to get familiar / get to know you.\u201d Meeldiv kohtuda \u2013 Nice to meet you. Greet"
